Letter from the Pinghu Maoba Hospital

Having recently read the news in your newspaper on February 20th about the Pinghu Hospital being vandalized and demanding money, it does not correspond to the facts. On the morning of the 16th of this month, a soldier from the local security department came to our hospital for treatment. Due to a misunderstanding caused by a language barrier, there was a minor argument. After clarification, he was treated and left. The so-called vandalism of the hospital, assault on the dean, and destruction of the sedan chair are all untrue. We respectfully request a correction to reflect the truth. Respectfully, Pinghu Maoba Hospital, February 21st.

Education News

Important News

The Experts' Meeting of the China Vocational Education Society in Suzhou (II)

The proceedings of the experts' meeting held by the China Vocational Education Society in Suzhou have been compiled and reported in yesterday's newspaper. However, the program for the second day's meeting and tour has been slightly changed from the original plan, as described below:

▲Details of the Second Day

At 7:30 a.m. on the 22nd, the participants boarded a boat from the back gate of the Garden Hotel. Chairman Liu Zhanen opened the meeting and reported that each participant would first present their opinions, limited to three minutes. A fine would be imposed for exceeding the time limit. The boat passed through Qi Shi Street and landed to visit the Provincial Agricultural Implement Manufacturing Factory, where breakfast was served. At 10:00 a.m., the participants passed through Muzhi Town and visited the People's Education Center, and toured the Yan Garden. Due to time constraints, they did not visit the Lingyan Mountain scenic spot, which is two or three miles from the town. They disembarked for lunch, which was provided by the Shijia Restaurant in the town. At a little after 1:00 p.m., they arrived at the Guangfu Town pier, where they were welcomed by soldiers and police. District Chief Zhang Shiyi, Public Security Bureau Chief Xu Mengling, and local leaders such as Gu Hengru hosted the group. They took 37 pre-hired sedan chairs to Situ Temple. After arriving at the temple, they admired the ancient and peculiar old cypress trees inscribed by Emperor Qianlong and then went to the Shengen Temple, where the old monk Tieqiao led them to the Huanyuan Pavilion for tea and snacks. The monk also showed them the Zhou Bianzhong of various countries and the calligraphy of famous people, which are rarely shown. Cai Yuanpei and Huang Renzhi were invited to write poems. Later, they climbed the artificial mountain to view Taihu Lake and also re-enacted the scene of Emperor Qianlong's throne. When descending the mountain, Wu Tingjie, the Guangxi Governor, arrived with his family. The reporter stayed briefly to take a photo of them. On the way back by boat, the discussion continued until a little after 9:00 p.m. Most of the participants took rickshaws to the station from the Xin Yuan Men to depart from Suzhou. Each location along the way was photographed by the museum for commemoration.

Photo of the Experts of the China Vocational Education Society Visiting the Jiangsu Provincial Agricultural Implement Manufacturing Factory

(Taken by this museum)

On that day, the county government dispatched six police officers to patrol the waterways along the way, and the water police patrolled the boat in shifts. There were also soldiers and police protecting the participants on land, so the journey was very safe.

The issues discussed on the boat included vocational guidance, agriculture, industry, commerce, and supplementary education. All of them have been resolved one by one. However, the issue of women's education will be discussed later because of the lack of female experts at this meeting. Finally, a temporary proposal was passed to request the Jiangsu Provincial Government to establish a rural police training institute. For the commemoration of this conference in Suzhou, the Shanren Bridge along the way was selected to establish a rural improvement society. Zhang Zhongren, a local resident, was appointed as the chairman, and Jiang Wenyu, Hu Chunzao, Liao Nancai, Shen Yinquan, Wu Guanghan, a local Li, and Huang Renzhi and Yao Huiquan from the society were appointed as members to prepare for the implementation. The fines for exceeding the time limit for expressing opinions during the meeting (only a few copper coins) were handed over to the chairman as the starting funds for the preparation.

▲Major Issues Resolved

(1) The proposal for the planning and design department of the society to engage in the design business of various agencies was resolved to first pilot small industries with semi-mechanical and semi-manual labor. If it is effective, then design for others. (2) Proposal to promote rural sideline occupations. (3) Proposal to pay attention to nearby land reclamation projects. (4) Proposal to promote small handicrafts. The above three proposals were approved. (5) Proposal for each industry to run its own vocational schools. It was resolved that schools that have already been established should be vocationalized, and those that have not been established should be promoted to establish them. (6) Improving existing occupations. It was resolved that people should first be sent to study the content of the occupations and guide the improvement methods. (7) Colonial border issue. It was resolved that the issue should first be promoted and publicized in writing, and the schools should organize border research societies to carry out the work effectively. (8) What methods should be used to train young people's thinking? It was resolved that self-improvement, pragmatism, hard work, and physical exercise should be the four major goals, and breaking the vanity of seeking promotion and fortune should be the key point. (5) What should be the methods of practical training in commercial subjects? It was resolved that hypothetical internships, contracted stores, and on-site trials can be used in conjunction. In addition, (1) schools should be run, (2) schools should concurrently operate agriculture, industry, and commerce, (3) schools should cooperate with vocational training, and (4) vocational institutions should be encouraged to run schools. Students should be required to serve for one year after graduation before being issued a diploma, especially in vocational schools and normal schools. The Ministry of Education should be consulted. (10) The proposal that the curriculum should be reduced and more practical opportunities should be provided in the last year of commercial subjects. (11) The proposal that vocational school students should first have a semester of practical training before being taught. (12) The proposal that commercial school students should pay attention to appearance and service ethics. The above three proposals were approved. (13) The proposal that the promotion of new agricultural tools often affects the livelihood of coolie farmers, and what measures should be taken to remedy this? It was resolved that sideline occupations should be promoted. (14) The proposal that compulsory education often encounters difficulties due to family livelihood issues, and how should this be resolved? It was resolved that morning classes, mobile schools, and half-day schools should be adopted, and a principle should be established: (1) Compulsory schools should not allow children to leave rural life until they have developed their abilities. (2) Compulsory education must strive to reduce the burden on families. (15) How to cultivate talents for implementing rural improvement in order to develop improvement projects? It was resolved that a suitable location should be designated to use local materials. (16) The proposal to request the Jiangsu Provincial Government's Department of Civil Affairs and Department of Agriculture and Mining to pilot a rural police training institute in Zhenjiang County was resolved to be submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for review by the society after drafting a plan. (17) Should the society organize a public unemployment relief committee to study and implement public unemployment relief projects? It was resolved that the committee could be organized in cooperation with various agencies. (18) Should the vocational guidance center run a correspondence course to provide further education for young people who already have jobs or are about to take jobs? It was resolved that a pilot program could be implemented according to the plan. (19) Should the society recruit ordinary employees from various stores and factories in Shanghai to establish a morning school to teach Chinese, applied writing, applied English, and bookkeeping? It was resolved that it was appropriate. (20) The society has an affiliated Tongwen School that enrolls 40 students, assigns books for them to read, and provides face-to-face instruction once a week. If there are any questions about reading, they can send letters for answers, and essays and writing are corrected by the school. Every half month or month, all the students are gathered at the society for lectures. Is this method appropriate, and should another lecture be compiled? It was resolved that it was appropriate, and the lecture notes should be prepared in cooperation with the correspondence course. (21) Vocational education urgently needs to be promoted. In the current situation, should it be promoted universally or selectively? Which areas should be the first to start? It was resolved that it should be promoted selectively, starting with the seven regions of Liaoning, Beiping, Hankou, Guangzhou, Xi'an, Zhangjiakou, and Baotou. (22) What should be the method of starting, and what work should be done in the first step? It was resolved that publicity, investigation, research, and training of personnel should be done. (23) How can young women in various places be made aware of the need to seek employment? It was resolved that it should start with publicity, with the principle of serving the community without hindering family affairs. All cases related to women's vocational education should be submitted to the society's Women's Vocational Education Committee for discussion. (24) The proposal to establish a rural experimental area at Shanren Bridge was resolved to appoint Zhang Zhongren, Li Yinquan, Hu Chunzao, Wu Guanghan, Liao Nancai, Jiang Wenyu, and Kong Jun as preparatory committee members to conduct investigations and start immediately. (25) The proposal to request the central government to implement a policy of industrial and commercial guarantees to benefit the development of domestic goods and the future of talents was resolved to be implemented. (26) The proposal to request the central and provincial governments to jointly organize a talent cultivation committee with relevant official agencies was resolved to be implemented. (27) Should the society submit opinions to the National Assembly? It was resolved to be handled by the Affairs Department.

Local News

The County Education Bureau Convened a Meeting of District Principals Yesterday

The Shanghai County Education Bureau convened a meeting of district principals yesterday afternoon at 2:00 p.m. The attendees were Zhu Hange from the first district, Director Shi from the second district, Zheng Guozhai from the third district, Yang Huiming from the fourth district, Niu Zhiyi from the fifth district, and Lin Qing from the sixth district. Zhu Hange was elected as the chairman. The agenda was as follows: 1. Reporting matters: (1) The provisional funds allocated to each school are set at 5% of the total for the year. Those who have used up all the funds in the first semester may not apply for more funds in the current semester. (2) It is not necessary to remake the inventory of school equipment and books. Any new items should be added at any time. (3) The work report issued by the department must still be filled out and reported every month, and attention should be paid to the following points to ensure timely reporting. (Write clearly and report two copies by mail in an envelope by the 10th of each month.) The school affairs report will be suspended for the current semester. The number of students attending and the reasons for student absences should be filled in the teaching section of the work report, and social activities should be filled in the other sections of the work report. (4) Those who have not filled out and submitted the equipment survey form should do so as soon as possible. (5) Various examination forms issued by the bureau must be processed immediately. (6) The methods for examining grades have been formulated by the research association (see the 35th issue of the monthly magazine). (7) A science and mathematics teaching aids exhibition will be held this semester. Please prepare for it. The dates are May 30th and 31st. The location is Beiqiao Primary School. The funding is a subsidy of two yuan per school for the elementary level (issued after the exhibits are submitted). (8) A visit will be held in early April of this semester. One person from each elementary school and one person from every two elementary schools will be selected, excluding substitute teachers. (9) The academic competition will still be held this semester. All fifth-grade students from elementary schools are designated to participate. (10) New principals and teachers who have not filled out the bureau's survey card must fill it out and submit their diplomas for verification. (11) The school status survey form, the faculty and staff survey form, and the student list must be filled out and submitted by March 10th. The standards and implementation methods for moral education must be written separately and attached. (11) The department's order to increase the number of students in rural primary schools and pay attention to the actual number of students attending. Schools with too few students must be merged. The standard is at least 30 students. Those who do not meet the standard may be cut or closed down. (13) Each school should immediately set up a way to enroll students and prepare for the opening of the affiliated public school. The opening date is March 2nd. The meeting date of the Social Education Association is March 1st. The locations of the affiliated public schools are: 1st Jucao, 2nd Ziteng, 3rd Zigang, 4th Mengjin, 5th Xicun, 6th Daonan, 7th Yuxiu, 8th Tangmin, 9th Sanmin, 15th Quan, 11th Paima, 12th Chenhang, 13th Tangqiao, 14th Zhenxin, 15th Dongqiao. (14) The specified forms (19 types) The names are listed in the 25th issue of the monthly magazine, page 52, and should be prepared one by one. (15) Each district elementary school should elect one person to participate in the local education research association. The research association has travel funds. The provisional regulations are in the 32nd issue of the monthly magazine. (17) Tuition fees should be collected responsibly by each principal. (17) The schedule must be submitted to the bureau for review within one week. 2. Elect one representative to attend the research association (all district elementary schools). 3. Distribute items: School affairs diary, one copy per school; work report, ten copies per school; status survey form (12), one copy per school; faculty and staff survey form, one copy per school. The above must be submitted to the bureau by March 10th. Student roster, one copy per school; survey card, equipment survey form.

Vocational Guidance Center Seeks Specialists

The Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center has recently been entrusted by a certain university in the Northeast to hire a professor of mechanics who is proficient in English, can design various machines, and can guide graduation theses and mechanical experiments. The monthly salary is 300 yuan. There is an urgent need for people. If there are talents who have studied mechanics in Europe and the United States and are willing to do so, they should go to the center to discuss the matter in person as soon as possible. The center believes that the most important thing in vocational guidance is testing. Previously, Dr. Shen Youqian, an expert in psychological testing, and Mr. Zheng Wenhan were invited to compile a general military affairs test. It has already been compiled. Now, Dr. Shen is starting to edit a kind of interest test. This test method completely imitates the various professional jobs, entertainment courses, and other items of the E.K. Strong Jr. Vocational Intereit Bland in the United States, and integrates the test materials. Those who are tested indicate their likes and dislikes for each item to observe their professional interests. This test is planned to be tried out in various banks, factories, and schools for guidance on further education and employment.

Expansion of Changming Art College

The Changming Art College, run by Mr. Wang Yiting, has achieved remarkable results in one year. Now, because the original school building is not enough, the entire school has been found near the South Railway Station, with more than 40 Western-style houses, lush flowers and trees, and exquisite arrangement. It can accommodate four or five hundred people, and there is a large sports field with open grassland and fresh air. It is truly a suitable place to cultivate art talents.

Jinnan Soccer & Zhenru Basketball Teams' Philippine Expedition (12)

(Special Correspondent Wen Chu, from Manila)

丨 Soccer Team 6th Battle 丨丨2-1 Victory Over Colombia

At 5:00 PM on February 10th, the Jinnan Soccer team played against Colombia, winning 2 to 1.

The Luo Family General Makes First Meritorious Achievement

Both sides chose their goal; we had the advantage of facing away from the sun. The opposing team was called "Club," but in reality, it was composed of elite players selected from various teams. Everyone was filled with spirit, seeking to wash away the shame of repeated defeats in previous days. Therefore, at the start of the battle, they launched a fierce attack. Our side, riding the momentum of successive victories, did not show weakness either. Within five minutes, General Hei displayed his iron-head skills, and General Luo demonstrated his long-legged ability. The headbutt missed, but the long leg successfully connected, and the ball went into the net. Having captured the first line of defense, their courage was increased a hundredfold.

The Enemy's Counterattack Recaptures Territory

Although the enemy suffered an initial setback, their spirit was not diminished. After the left forward received the ball, their center forward immediately took a shot from more than ten yards away from our castle. Although the goalkeeper deflected it, the ball had already crossed the line, and it was ruled valid. The first line of defense they gained was retaken in less than five minutes. How can we underestimate the enemy's strength?

▲ Two Armies Charge, Displaying Divine Power

With the score tied, this was (the first game after the Battle of Ratsat Team, the enemy's only result). Naturally, everyone was filled with spirit. General Luo received a pass from Mei Hongbao, ran forward, and took a kneeling shot, but unfortunately, it went too high and over the net, missing a great opportunity. From then on, the enemy's forwards all strove to display their skills, switching from defense to offense, coordinating passes, and attacking from far and near. Their figures were frequently seen in our territory. Fortunately, the central pillar, General Huo Fa, and the left and right defenders, Chen Jiaqiu and Liang Shutang, were stationed at the three cities, providing thorough support. To advance two more cities, we had the copper-headed and iron-legged Generals and Jiang Shanjing, whose defenses were solid. Therefore, the enemy's attacks were all unsuccessful. Our side, taking advantage of their slight fatigue, issued orders and also pressed towards the enemy's territory. At one point, General Hei received support from the rear and kicked fiercely from the right. The ball rolled along the ground and was pushed out by the enemy goalkeeper, but center forward Dai got the ball and immediately passed it to Liang Shutang, who passed it to Fu Hexuan. Fu dribbled forward, about to display his skill of "flying across the Yangtze River," when the opposing center back kicked the ball out of bounds. Before long, the enemy forward intercepted the ball and dribbled it quickly forward. Our forwards were busy in the enemy territory and couldn't rush back in time. Fortunately, the central pillar of defense responded quickly and drove the enemy back. This was a period of mixed combat. When the first half ended, the score was tied at one to one.

▲ The Two Sides Compete to Take the Lead

After the break, the battle resumed, and the competition was even more intense, as each side wanted to take the lead. The enemy took advantage of our army's vulnerability and charged straight in. Fortunately, Generals Ma and Jiang rushed back desperately, averting the danger. Our side got the ball and did not show weakness either. Center forward Dai dribbled straight up and passed it to Mei Hongbao, who passed it back. Dai took a fierce shot, but it went too high and out of bounds. The enemy got the ball and launched an attack. The right forward aimed at the city and shot, but goalkeeper Xie saved it. Center forward Dai got the ball and passed it to General Hei. These two tiger generals advanced side by side. The crowd all had hopes of success. Before aiming at the enemy goal, it was kicked out by their defender. The enemy forward took the opportunity to loft a high ball, but goalkeeper Xie rushed out and kicked it away. Chen Bingxiang intercepted it and immediately passed it to General Hei, who headed it, but it was also caught and kicked out by the enemy goalkeeper. In these few minutes, back and forth, each side displayed their fighting skills.

▲ Chen and Luo's Collaboration Achieves Miraculous Success

As the stalemate continued, the sun was setting, and time was running out. If they were not careful and the enemy scored another goal, the reputation of Jinnan University would be greatly affected. The audience was anxiously worried for our side. However, the Jinnan students, with the efforts of the crowd, used an unexpected tactic. General Hei got the ball from the rear and quickly passed it to General Luo. Luo didn't rush, but attacked the ball from the rear right and kicked it into the net. The cheers that had been suppressed for so long erupted from the overseas Chinese. From then on, although the enemy repeatedly launched counterattacks, our side was a hundred times more spirited and fought even harder. When the game ended, they won 2 to 1.

▲ Receiving the Winning Prize on the Spot

Before the game, the general secretary of the Charity Association announced that a large silver cup had been prepared as a prize for the winning team of this game. As a result, it should be won by our side. The prize was awarded on the spot by the Director of the Department of Agricultural Affairs and Natural Resources. Center forward Dai received it on behalf of the team, and the entire team chanted the victory slogan to conclude the event.

Financial Specie Declines Sharply

▲ Repeated Ups and Downs ··· Extreme Fluctuations

▲ Thirty Taels Difference Yesterday, February 23rd, the decline of specie intensified, the state of affairs became extremely chaotic, with high to low transformations drastic like a madman's, the nerve-wracking fluctuations exceeding ten taels. Throughout the day, the difference reached thirty taels, with no certainty, ultimately falling more than ten taels. This was likely due to the trend of remittances declining significantly, with the posted price increasing by one and a half steps. As for market trading, it was completely different, particularly complex and chaotic. In the morning, Hengxing, Yuansheng, and Yuansheng bought and sold again, while Yuanmao, Yongxin, Hengyuan, and Tai were all buying in. Hengxing, Zhifeng, Yongqian, and Changxiang generally sold out. The overseas silver market rose the day before yesterday, so the gold price fell slightly. Suddenly, large traders enthusiastically bought, soaring upwards, rising sharply by more than ten taels, almost reaching 770 taels. Instantly, large traders such as Hengxing, Yuansheng, Yuansheng, Qianchangxiang, etc., began to sell because foreign exchange suddenly loosened, and there was talk of conflicting news about Sino-American loans, suggesting the silver price might rise again. Therefore, people were frightened, and with the confluence of winds and waves, it plummeted by thirty taels, suddenly falling below forty taels. At noon, there was a turning and easing, and it was raised by ten taels, seemingly due to the news that spot goods could be exported. In short, the market formed a multi-faceted pattern due to atmospheric influences. The after-market also had a ten-tael rebound, hovering around fifty taels, with different firms seeking various supplies. However, remittances remained loose and abundant, and spot [gold] bars initially showed signs of expansion, so the price of spot should be more than fifty taels higher than the forward price. It is expected that the large bars will rise again this morning, but there is no market for silver because yesterday (23rd) was a holiday in America, and work was suspended.

Silver Market Slightly Develops

▲ Market Overview Presenting an opportunity. Commercial practice is that every New Year, businesses operate at half capacity, so the market is more relaxed than usual. Although the Gregorian calendar is used this time, old customs are still difficult to eradicate. As a result, there is compliance in public but defiance in private, continuing as in previous years. In the end, the market was sluggish, starting to show a slight opportunity yesterday. Bank receipts and payments have been slightly reported, but the money market still operates only half a day, so there is no way to develop it.

▲ Silver gradually rises. The silver price has the potential for progress, so it rises gradually every day. Yesterday, it was 7 qian, 2 fen, 4 li, an increase of 3 hao, 7 and a half from the previous day's higher price. The situation is still promising, but with the imminent arrival of the god of wealth silver, which all ports have been accustomed to, it is still possible that the silver price will weaken. The early silver market was still white loan [interest-free], and there was no market at noon as usual, and the clearing rate was also unavailable.

▲ Auxiliary coins rise in the south and fall in Guangdong. The small silver coins in Jiangnan rose yesterday to 6 qian, 8 fen, 5 li, an increase of 1 fen and 2 li from the previous day. 4,000 jiao [units] were easily sold in the early market. The small silver coins in Guangdong, on the other hand, fell by 4 li and 2 hao and a half, to 6 qian, 6 fen, 3 li, 7 hao and a half. 175,000 jiao [units] were traded. Grains: Deteriorating Environment Causes Flour Market to Plummet

Yesterday, the flour market, after opening in the morning and afternoon, suddenly showed signs of a sharp decline in prices for all months. The rise and fall of the current market have completely deviated from the actual situation of the flour market itself. Based on the circumstances, before the weekend opening, due to spot goods and gold prices, it caused outsiders to rush to buy, and the market atmosphere was strong. When the price opened yesterday, the quoted price of foreign wheat was slightly lower by 126 corners. The gold market, because of the hope of a large loan agreement, also plummeted, causing people to unanimously look down and sell vigorously. The inexperienced bulls have no courage to enter further in this reversal of the environment, and because the large short positions belong to the factories and speculative short selling, there is a difference between getting on and off the bed, so they are calm and composed as usual. The factories were still actively selling during both the morning and afternoon sessions, and floating bulls were rushing to get out, so the market continued to plummet. As a result, the current month fell 7 cents compared to the previous weekend, March fell 6 cents and 2.5 mills, April and May fell 6.5 cents, June fell 8 cents and 7.5 mills, and July fell 8.5 cents, it is said.

Wheat Market Plummets Sharply

▲ Especially severe in forward months... plummeting ¥0.024

Yesterday, futures wheat prices for all months saw a strange and sharp decline. Because the quoted price of foreign wheat was slightly lower, and the exchange rate also continued to fall, people generally speculated that the fall in the overall price following the conclusion of the large loan was also expected. With this phenomenon, the future exchange rate will relax, and ordering foreign wheat for delivery will naturally have to be activated again. Therefore, people's hearts were greatly disturbed, and sellers in the industry were even more eager to sell, and the situation became more turbulent. The trend of current growth and decline still needs to be based on foreign countries as a guide. It is found that if the foreign exchange rate changes after this kind of situation of easy rise and easy fall, some disturbances will still be unavoidable. Trading was very active throughout the day, reaching more than 600 vehicles. As a result, the current month fell ¥0.013 on the previous day, March fell ¥0.013, April fell ¥0.015, May fell ¥0.018, June fell ¥0.019, and July alone fell a huge ¥0.024, it is said.

Silk and Tea: Shanghai Silk Factories Resuming Operations One After Another

Due to the plunge in European sales of factory silk last year, Shanghai's silk factories suffered from low capital and exhausted funds, facing bankruptcy and total shutdown. Although some factories tried hard to resume work, they opened and stopped intermittently. At the beginning of last month, more than 40 factories borrowed cocoons from the financial sector to start their machines. Around the end of the lunar year, female workers voluntarily stopped working and refused to go to the factories, so the factories had no choice but to temporarily suspend work. Now that the old lunar new year has passed, and the government's silk industry bonds are about to be issued, the factories are eager to resume operations. Yesterday, more than ten factories, such as Ruilun and Xinyi, had already started their machines, it is said.

Sui'an Zhenmei Tea Actively Being Sold in England

Yesterday, in the foreign firm tea market, Sui'an Zhenmei green tea, sold by British firms like Jardine Matheson and Concord, because the Russian firm's assistance association is about to open, buying has resumed. More than 610 boxes were traded throughout the city, and the selling price was unchanged from the settlement period. More than 1,000 boxes of Gongxi green tea were purchased by British firms like Baitou Zhuangfu yesterday for sale in ports such as Persia and Mumbai, it is said.

British Envoy to Arrive Today

▲ Ministry of Foreign Affairs Orders Proper Care

The Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs received a telegram from the Ministry yesterday, stating that the British Envoy to China, Lampson, had departed from Singapore to Shanghai and then to Beijing to negotiate legal rights issues with Minister Wang. He is expected to arrive in Shanghai around the 24th of this month (today) and will then transfer to Beijing by train. British Consul-General's Car Collides, Mr. Brenan Injured

▲ But Not Severely, Early Recovery Expected

According to the North-China Daily News, British Consul-General Brenan was returning to his office by car after attending a Washington's Birthday celebration banquet at the American Club the other night. When the car reached the intersection of Henan Road and Jiujiang Road, an outbound taxi rushed from the west. The two cars could not avoid each other and collided. The bodies of the cars were damaged, and Mr. Brenan was also severely shaken and injured. After returning to his office, he urgently called a doctor for examination. One or two ribs have been bruised, but the injury is not very serious and an early recovery is expected, it is said.

The Outline of Business Tax Remains Largely Unchanged

▲ The Ministry of Finance Replies to the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce by Telegram

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce previously sent a letter and telegram to the Ministry of Finance from various chambers of commerce, stating that the outline for collecting business tax formulated by the Ministry of Finance was inconsistent with the original plan resolved at the National Likin Abolition Conference in 1928. They specifically telegraphed the Ministry of Finance for an explanation. Yesterday, the Federation received a reply telegram stating, "To Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the Shanghai National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, et al.: I have read the Fish-Dai telegram in its entirety. The outline for collecting business tax passed by the Executive Yuan and implemented in various provinces and cities this time is the original plan resolved at the National Likin Abolition Conference in 1928. The points of amendment only include the deletion of the seven characters 'or hinder the development of domestic goods' under Article 4, which contains matters that should be banned, and the amendment of the two characters 'examination' in 'establishment of a business tax review committee' in Article 5 to 'deliberation.' The remaining clauses have not changed much. The inconsistencies mentioned in the telegram are probably due to misunderstandings. As for the draft business regulations of Jiangsu Province, the province has been approved to send a note to the Ministry. If the business classification, tax standard, and tax rate exceed the provisions of the outline and supplementary measures ordered by the Ministry, they should be reviewed and amended separately, and the province should be notified to instruct the Department of Finance to comply with the regulations. You should immediately inform all chambers of commerce accordingly. [Seal of] the Ministry of Finance."

The Joint Association of Silk and Satin Merchants in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai Announces Compliance with the Order to Pay Business Tax

▲ Because the Government Has Clearly Defined It As a Daily Necessity for Common People

The Joint Association of Silk and Satin Guilds in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai announced to the various silk and satin industry groups: "The various silk and satin industry groups in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai previously reported that the business tax rates stipulated by the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces exceeded the outline stipulated by the Ministry, exceeding the maximum limit of 2/1000 by more than 7 times, which was impossible to bear. Representatives were sent to Beijing to petition and announced in newspapers to the silk industry groups and merchants in various provinces and cities that in order to respect the central government's orders and protect the survival of the silk industry, until the business tax rates of silk and satin in various provinces and cities are revised in accordance with the outline stipulated by the Ministry to a maximum of no more than 2/1000, payment should be temporarily suspended. Now, on February 18, we respectfully read the approval from the Ministry of Industry, the Shanghai Silk and Satin Industry Association telegram read: 'We have checked and inquired about the case of requesting a reduction in the business tax on silk fabrics in Zhejiang Province. We have added our opinions and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for review and instructions and telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Government to handle it. Now we have received instructions from the Executive Yuan, which read: "I have read the report. It is said that silk and satin are special national products and need protection, and their uses are also daily necessities for common people. Please instruct all provinces to collect business tax on this item, and the tax rate shall not exceed 2/1000 to protect it." This is in line with the previous order from the Central Government to relieve the silk weaving industry and should be approved. Please order the Ministry of Finance and the governments of all provinces and cities to comply with and handle it accordingly." We hereby notify you accordingly.' On the same day, we also received a telegram from the Ministry of Finance stating, 'We have checked that Article 1 of the Business Tax Outline of various provinces states that silk factories and silk factories are excluded from the special taxes collected by the central government. If the central government has already collected special taxes, all manufacturing industries and the wholesale industries directly established by them can be exempted from business tax. The wholesale and retail industries in the goods sales industry should still be collected to show the distinction. In addition to separately amending the draft business tax regulations of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and other provinces, and notifying the Provincial Government to instruct the Department of Finance to comply with the regulations, we hereby notify you accordingly.' It can be seen that the central government has foresight and is committed to protecting the silk industry. Our Association has carefully interpreted the approval order. One says that 'silk and satin are special national products and need protection,' another says that 'their uses are also daily necessities for common people,' and a third says that 'it is in line with the previous order from the Central Government to relieve the silk weaving industry.' It is already clearly indicated and affirmed by the central government that silk and satin are daily necessities and not luxury businesses, and the wording is clear and obvious. Our provincial and municipal governments can understand the virtue and comply with the order to regulate the business tax rate of the silk and satin industry to below 2/1000. Since the government can understand the difficulties of the silk industry and provide extra protection, the silk merchants should do their best to fulfill their tax obligations and comply with the order to pay taxes. This is hereby announced, and we hope you will take note of it. The Preparatory Committee of the Joint Association of Silk and Satin Guilds in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai, address: 96 Beijing Road, Shanghai."

Various Industries Request Reduction of Business Tax

▲ Ham Industry: The Ham Industry Association in this city, because the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces have stipulated that the business tax rate for the industry is collected at 15/1000, which exceeds the provisions of the outline, and the business is unable to bear the burden, specifically sent representatives Cai Xiaohe, Zhu Hanwo, Xin Wenxuan, etc., to Beijing yesterday with representatives from the Suzhou Salted Meat and Ham and Egg Industry Association to petition the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry separately, it is said.

▲ Western Paint Industry: The Western Paint Industry Association telegraphed Hu Hanmin, President of the Legislative Yuan of the National Government, Finance Minister Song Ziwen, and Industry Minister Kong Xiangxi yesterday, requesting a reduction in the business tax rate. The original telegram briefly stated: "The tax rate of 10/1000 for paint is an erroneous calculation, causing great consternation. We hereby express our grievances and telegraphically request your government, yuan, and ministries to consider the difficulties of the business, make every effort to correct it, and order the Shanghai Municipal Government, Finance Bureau, and Business Tax Preparatory Office to comply with Article 4 of the Ministry-promulgated Outline for Paint Sales Tax and reduce it to 1/1000, which shall not exceed the standard of 2/1000, in order to alleviate business difficulties and maintain people's livelihood. We are extremely grateful and sincere, and we knock on your door. The Shanghai Western Paint Industry Association bows respectfully."

Qingdao Match Industry Representatives Went to Beijing Yesterday to Petition

▲ Send Letters to Various Sectors Asking for Consistent Assistance

▲ Do Not Allow Swedish Merchants to Succeed in Their Invasion

The Qingdao Match Industry Federation, because the consolidated tax on matches is collected too heavily, convened meetings several times to discuss and decided to send Qu Jiantang and Sun Juncheng as representatives to petition the Ministry of Finance in Beijing. Mr. Sun and Mr. Qu arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday and took a train to Beijing last night. It is said that the Qingdao City used phosphorus sulfide matches, which were mostly Japanese goods. Every year, the money was lost overseas, which was impossible to count. Over the past year, local people have raised funds to start domestic match factories in order to resist foreign goods. All products are relatively excellent. In addition to supplying the entire Qingdao City, the remaining amount can be transported to Tianjin and various counties in the interior of Shandong Province. Invisibly, a lot of interests and rights have been recovered. This time, the central government implemented a unified tax. The tax rate on phosphorus sulfide matches is as high as 40%. All manufacturers are unable to bear the heavy tax burden. The factories in the city will all close down one after another. Tens of thousands of men and women workers will also lose their livelihoods. The Federation appointed Yu and two others to petition the Ministry of Finance to show sympathy for the difficulties of the domestic industry and reduce the consolidated tax rate, it is said. The Federation also sent letters to colleagues and people from all walks of life, hoping to provide assistance based on the principle of helping each other in the same boat. The letter is recorded as follows: "Respected sirs, for years, the match industry in our country has been invaded by foreign merchants externally and suffered from heavy donations and taxes internally. It is in imminent danger. If there is no corresponding maintenance method, it will inevitably perish together. Since the first day of this year, after the government implemented the abolition of likin, the accumulated malpractices over the years have been cleared, and all Chinese people have been celebrating. However, after the abolition of likin, unified taxes will be used to offset it, but the unified tax rate is too high, and it is really difficult for businesses and people to bear. The disadvantages are described as follows: (1) The unified tax rate is too high, and manufacturers are unable to pay the advance. According to the Department's regulations on unified taxes, matches are collected at 7 yuan and 5 jiao in national currency per large box (7,200 boxes with a length of more than 43 mm and less than 52 mm), which refers to safety matches. However, the length of phosphorus sulfide matches (commonly known as red-headed matches) in Shandong is only 40 mm, and each large box is usually 14,400 boxes, with a tax of 15 yuan, which will be nearly half of the value of the goods. For small factories, the cost is only about 10,000 yuan. If 20 boxes are shipped per day, 300 yuan of tax must be paid, which is 9,000 yuan per month. The large factories that ship 100 boxes a day have to pay more than 40,000 yuan in taxes every month. According to the industry's practice of selling goods, it takes at least three or four months to receive payment after shipping out of the factory, and some even take more than half a year. How can they have so much power to pay such a huge amount in advance? (2) The unified tax rate is unfair. The tax rate stipulated in the unified tax regulations is that cotton yarn is taxed at no more than 5%, cement is taxed at no more than 8-9%, and flour is only 2%. However, each box of phosphorus sulfide matches (14,400 boxes) sells for less than 40 yuan, and the tax is 15 yuan, so the unified rate exceeds 40%. In terms of matches, the price of 7,200 boxes of safety matches is the same as the price of 14,400 boxes of phosphorus sulfide matches, but the unified tax paid is twice as much for phosphorus sulfide matches. The government promotes industry and should reduce the tax rate on necessities for the daily use of the poor to enrich people's livelihood. However, the tax amount set is several times higher than others, which is difficult to understand. (3) Matches are related to people's livelihood. Phosphorus sulfide matches are purely necessary for farmers, workers, and the poor, so the selling price is low. According to the annual average calculation, the selling price per large box is only 34-5 yuan. Now, due to the surge in gold prices, expensive raw materials, and the gradual increase in the cost of artificial life, the current cost calculation is more than 50 yuan. In addition, the economic invasion of Sweden is selling cheaply everywhere. The match selling price has no way to increase. If 15 yuan is levied per box, it will not only be difficult to sell, but the poor will be limited by the economy and will inevitably cause a fire-fighting system, which is not the ultimate intention of the Prime Minister to promote people's livelihood. (4) The unified tax is just to help Sweden's invasion succeed. Sweden has always held the ambition to annex the world's matches. In recent years, it has acquired many Japanese match factories in our country, sold them at a loss, and carried out an invasion. The Chinese factories with weak capital have repeatedly received government relief, such as reduced railway transportation, etc., and are still not enough to compete with them. If this major unified tax is levied again, it will inevitably lead to shutdowns and closures, wouldn't it be to drive away birds for the sake of the forest, turning to help the Swedish merchants succeed in their invasion? Given the above four points, our Association has consulted repeatedly, but there is no way. We can only ask the government to allow the implementation of the match monopoly system in the three northeastern provinces to provide relief. We have now sent representatives to Beijing to petition, hoping that you will provide consistent assistance based on the friendship of helping each other in the same boat.

Pan Gongzhan's Speech on the General Situation of Social Administration in Shanghai

The Shanghai YMCA's Municipal Research Society held a speech by Mr. Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, the day before yesterday (Saturday). On that day, the Social Affairs Bureau first displayed 72 statistical charts from various departments, as well as 37 types of publications of the bureau, arranged by Shao Songsheng and Xue Wenyuan of the bureau. Director Pan arrived at the meeting at 4 p.m. to give a speech, which was attended by more than 300 listeners and ended at around 6 p.m. The following is a transcript of his speech:

Today, I am honored to be invited by the YMCA's Municipal Research Society to speak on the general situation of social administration in Shanghai. As the Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, I have a duty to report on this type of issue. However, the term "social" has a very broad meaning and encompasses too much. To put it simply, matters handled by the central government, the provincial government, the municipal government, and the county government are all related to social affairs. People cannot exist independently of society, and therefore, prosperity, decline, rise, and fall are all closely related. Dr. Sun Yat-sen said, "Politics is the matter of the people, governance is management, and managing the affairs of the people is called politics." In other words, the affairs of the people are the affairs of society. Since the scope of society is so broad, why haven't we heard of social affairs bureaus in European and American countries, or a social affairs department in the central government? Even the Shanghai Municipal Council (工部局) and provincial governments have not established social affairs departments or offices. Why is there a social affairs bureau only in the municipal organization law? This type of title also exists in Japan. However, the social affairs bureau in Japan only manages matters related to public welfare, charity, and relief, which is different from the Social Affairs Bureau in our country's municipal organization law, which has the same name but different functions. According to the provisions of the municipal organization law, the municipal government has 24 functions, and the Social Affairs Bureau occupies 10 of them, almost half. In addition to agriculture, industry, commerce, public welfare, charity, and relief, education and public utilities are also within the functions of the Social Affairs Bureau according to the municipal organization law. Currently, education and public utilities in Shanghai have become independent agencies. After removing these two, the Social Affairs Bureau still occupies eight functions. The Social Affairs Bureau was established in August of the 17th year of the Republic of China (1928). To date, it has been two years and seven months. Before the Social Affairs Bureau, it was the Bureau of Agriculture, Industry, and Commerce, which was established in July of the 16th year of the Republic of China (1927). Speaking of the Social Affairs Bureau, it is just a two-and-a-half-year-old child. Even when combined with the Bureau of Agriculture, Industry, and Commerce, it is only a three-year-old child. In terms of qualifications, it can be said to be extremely immature. So, what are the achievements of the Social Affairs Bureau? This should first be observed from the perspective of its funding and time. Insufficient funding is truly like the ancient saying, "Even a clever woman cannot cook without rice." If the funding is sufficient, but the time is not enough, it is also difficult to expect rapid progress. People in society often have an incorrect judgment, believing that the municipal administration of the foreign concessions is progressing and becoming better every day, while the municipal administration of the Chinese area does not seem to have much progress. The reason for this cannot be blamed on the authorities. It should be known that the Public Concession has a very large income and a history of more than 80 years, while the municipal government only has a history of three and a half years. The difference in time is so great that it is, of course, impossible to catch up with their achievements. Now, I will report on the expenses of the Social Affairs Bureau over the years. In the 17th year of the Republic of China (1928), it was 12,495 yuan per month. In the 18th year of the Republic of China (1929), it was 16,373 yuan. In the 19th year of the Republic of China (1930), it was 19,431 yuan. In addition, the temporary expenses were 19,000 yuan in the 17th year of the Republic of China (1928), 22,000 yuan in the 18th year of the Republic of China (1929), and 28,000 yuan in the 19th year of the Republic of China (1930). Comparing the above figures, it is indeed increasing year by year. However, according to the distribution of the municipal government's financial resources over the years, it accounted for 5% when it was the Bureau of Agriculture, Industry, and Commerce in the 16th year of the Republic of China (1927), 4.3% after the reorganization into the Social Affairs Bureau in the 17th year of the Republic of China (1928), 4.5% in the 18th year of the Republic of China (1929), and 4.5% in the 19th year of the Republic of China (1930). This is because the municipal government's funding has increased year by year. The Social Affairs Bureau is one of the agencies under the municipal government, and its finances are less than one-twentieth, while the affairs it manages account for eight-twentieths. As for what the Social Affairs Bureau does in terms of agriculture, industry, and commerce, I will tell you separately. (A) Agriculture: Shanghai is entirely a metropolis. Why is agriculture still needed? It should be known that there are still fields in the areas around Shanghai that have not been developed into business districts. Furthermore, according to the trend of the world, cities must adopt the natural beauty of rural areas. Therefore, this point cannot be ignored. As a result, the Social Affairs Bureau is handling two agricultural matters. (1) Garden nursery: It has only been in operation for two years since it started, so there are not many trees that can be transplanted. It is estimated that the number of branches transplanted each year will be 1,650 in the 19th year of the Republic of China (1930), 110 in the 21st year of the Republic of China (1932), 1,590 in the 22nd year of the Republic of China (1933), 65,480 in the 23rd year of the Republic of China (1934), and 560,000 in the 24th year of the Republic of China (1935). (2) Agricultural experiment station: It specializes in researching the seeds of agricultural products, such as cotton, rice, beans, and wheat. In the future, if successful experiments are made, these seeds will be distributed to the countryside to promote good agricultural production and progress. However, because there is not much funding and the land is too small, it is planned to purchase more land and add manpower to expand it in the future. (B) Industry: In the industrial sector, there is an industrial goods testing institute, which has been established for two years and specializes in researching the improvement of industrial products. The start-up cost was 20,000 yuan, and the monthly recurring expenses were previously about 1,000 yuan, but have now been increased to 1,500 yuan. Since its establishment, the number of factories in Shanghai requesting tests has gradually increased, and it will need to be expanded in the future. After a comprehensive survey of factories in Shanghai in the 17th year of the Republic of China (1928), there were about 1,500 factories. The new additions and closures have not yet been investigated. It is because the knowledge of Chinese merchants is too simple, and they often suspect the personnel sent by government agencies for investigation, refusing them in every way, making it difficult to carry out an investigation. The difficulties are beyond description. (C) Commerce: In the commercial sector, the Social Affairs Bureau has conducted a comprehensive survey of the customs and practices of various industries to obtain a systematic standard in each industry and improve it. More than 50 industries have been surveyed. Here, I will take the pawnshop industry in Shanghai as an example. There are more than 500 pawnshops in Shanghai, but only 50 to 60 are under the jurisdiction of the municipal government, with the majority located within the concessions. The interest rates of pawnshops are as high as 6 to 9 percent per month. When the revolutionary army arrived in Shanghai in the 16th year of the Republic of China (1927), strict measures were taken to crack down on this high-interest exploitation. The Social Affairs Bureau conducted a survey of the industry and made regulations that the monthly interest rate for pawnshops should not exceed 2 percent, and the monthly interest rate for rough pawned items should not exceed 3 percent. After these regulations were made, those who did not understand thought that the Social Affairs Bureau still favored the pawnshop merchants and ignored the suffering of the common people. In fact, this is not the case. The nature of the pawnshop industry is to regulate the livelihood of the common people, which is a kind of commercial activity, different from ordinary lending. Ordinary lending is based on the amount of financial resources as the standard. If there is 1,000 yuan that can be lent, after the loan is used up, those who come later can be rejected. Pawnshops are not like this. If their personal financial resources are exhausted, they must borrow from the money industry to make ends meet. If so, then they must pay interest, plus expenses such as rent, food, and servants. They use their income to make up for their expenses, and merchants must always make a profit. Therefore, the Social Affairs Bureau weighed the situation and took into account the interests of the merchants on the one hand and the suffering of the common people on the other, so that both parties could benefit. However, the situation in the concessions remains the same. Although the Shanghai Municipal Council (工部局) and Chinese directors have been repeatedly consulted to crack down on high interest rates, the result is still zero. (D) Labor: In the labor sector, the Social Affairs Bureau has been looking at the living standards and wages of workers, and whether their income is sufficient to cover their living expenses. Since the beginning, 500 workers have been used as a standard, and people have been sent to their homes every day to register their daily expenses. After more than a year, an approximate figure was obtained. It is planned to conduct further investigations in the future to set a minimum price for wages in the future. As for the mediation work of the Social Affairs Bureau, it is entirely a passive work. Since its handling, disputes have gradually decreased. In the future, it is hoped that they will not occur at all, so that society can be peaceful and all industries can develop. The situation of the agricultural, industrial, and commercial administration of the Social Affairs Bureau has been described above. However, there are many other issues. If there is an opportunity in the future, I will continue to report to you on public welfare and charitable administration, and so on.

Shanghai County Government Meeting

▲57th Meeting

The Shanghai County Government held its 57th county government meeting at 2 p.m. yesterday, attended by Wang Li, Director of the Finance Bureau, Wu Wenhua, Director of the Construction Bureau, Shi She, Director of the Education Bureau, Chen Guozhen of the Public Security Bureau, and Ye Dezhen, Secretary of the County Government, Section Chief Yu Tanfen, Chairman Yan Shenyu, County Magistrate, and Recorder Hu Gongshou. After the usual formalities, the motions were discussed and resolved. (1) The County Construction Bureau proposed a draft of the County's Pre-Planned Table for the Restoration and Governance Preparation Period, please submit for decision. Resolved to approve with amendments. (2) The County Government submitted a motion from the County Construction Bureau regarding the proposed Afforestation Campaign Plan for this year, and how to regulate the disbursement of the campaign's budget. Resolved that the campaign expenses be limited to 50 yuan, to be disbursed from the County's Internal Affairs expenses. (3) The County Government submitted a motion in accordance with the Provincial Government's order to submit the local budget for the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931) by the deadline.
