Resolved: (A) The County's local finances are insufficient, and the County Agricultural Station has no funding. In the budget for the 19th year of the Republic of China (1930), funds were borrowed from the County's Internal Affairs expenses, making it difficult to carry out County affairs. It is proposed to request the Provincial Government to approve the levy of 5% on surplus grain transportation tax to fund agricultural improvement expenses. (B) The finances of each district are insufficient, and autonomous affairs are burdensome. It is proposed to levy a construction donation tax from the deed tax and brokerage tax, starting from the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931), and allocate it for district use. (C) A budget meeting will be convened at 10 a.m. this Thursday. (D) The Finance Bureau is designated to prepare a draft budget. (4)

The County Government submitted a motion from the County Public Security Bureau regarding the payment of expenses for wounded soldiers submitted by the garrison headquarters. The expenses have been settled, with actual expenses of 964.823 yuan, income of 699.44 yuan from the headquarters' rations, and a financial subsidy of 265.383 yuan. It is proposed to write off the expenses within the County's Internal Affairs expenses as per the case, please submit for decision. Resolved to write off the expenses as per the case. (5) The County Government submitted a motion regarding the County's implementation of the first step of the Clear Countryside Plan as ordered, focusing on publicity. It is proposed that the Education Bureau order the principals, teachers, and students of each school to convene meetings of parents and hold open-air speeches in order to assist. Resolved to order the Education Bureau to comply.

Navy Aircraft Manufacturing Bureau After Moving to Shanghai

▲Temporarily Using Jiangnan Shipyard for Office

▲Yesterday, Two Aircraft Were Test-Flown

The Navy Majiang Aircraft Manufacturing Bureau, after moving to Shanghai from Fujian the day before yesterday, is temporarily using the Jiangnan Shipyard for office because the building being constructed in the city has not yet been completed. All the staff and the Deputy Director, Zeng Yijing, are temporarily residing at the Jiangnan Shipyard. After the old warehouse is renovated, they will move in again. At 2 p.m. yesterday, He Jian and Jie Chengdong, instructors from the Naval Aviation Office of the city, flew two land-based aircraft, "Jiang" and "Jiangyang", from Hongqiao Airport to the airspace in front of the Gaochangmiao Aircraft Factory, soaring back and forth for more than an hour before returning slowly. It is reported that both the "Jiang" and "Jiangyang" aircraft were manufactured by the Majiang Aircraft Factory.

Aviation News

▲Two Seamen's Congress Delegates: The first National Seamen's Congress was held in Guangzhou last year. The second National Seamen's Congress this year is scheduled to be held in Shanghai. The venue is the Shanghai Seamen's Union General Assembly Hall on Fuzhou Road. The date has been agreed to be April 1st. Yesterday, the Shanghai Seamen's Union was discussing the selection of delegates to the second National Seamen's Congress. If the number of delegates is elected according to the number of members in each department, it would not be fair. Committee members Wang Yongsheng and others proposed that the delegates to this Congress should be elected according to department to avoid imbalance. After the decision is made, the branch unions across the country will be notified.

▲Nippon Yusen Kaisha Deficit and Layoffs: Nippon Yusen Kaisha suffered a total loss of 5 million yuan last year. This year, in order to tighten expenses, it must lay off employees again. It has telegraphed to branches across the country to send the list of employees to the head office for the purpose of employee retention. In addition, the company previously announced the recruitment of female attendants to serve on various ships. Later, the Shanghai branch received as many as four or five hundred letters of application. Some even held newspapers that reported the matter and went to the company to inquire about the examination dates. The inquiries were endless. The company considered that this matter was presided over by the head office in Japan and that the recruits were Japanese women, not Chinese women. Recently, there have been too many inquiries, and it is difficult to answer them all. It is planned to issue a correction notice to avoid those who are mistaken from running around in vain. The Shanghai branch does not recruit Chinese female waiters.

▲Shanghai-Ningbo Fee Increase Stalled: The San Gong Tong (三公同) company planned to increase the fare and passenger ticket for the Shanghai-Ningbo route by 20% from the 18th of this month to fund the escort team. This matter has aroused opposition from merchants in Ningbo, and the ship waiters have unanimously resisted. Recently, the Ship Waiters' Union has also petitioned the Ministry of Communications, requesting that the increase in fees by the three companies be stopped. Yesterday, the Ministry of Communications issued an order, ordering China Merchants, Sanbei, Ningshao, and others to submit the reasons for increasing the fare and passenger ticket and the reasons for adding the escort team by the deadline for review and decision. As a result, the fee increase on the 18th had to be postponed, and the escort police team did not board the ship. Negotiations are currently underway with all parties.

▲Northern Ports Frozen and Not Open: There have been two major cold spells in the North this month. The Baihe River has frozen again, and even the outside of Tanggu Port has solid ice. More than a dozen merchant ships in Tianjin Port are blocked by the ice. Yesterday, various shipping companies in Shanghai telegraphed to Tianjin to inquire. They received a reply saying that the solid ice in the Baihe River has not melted, and none of the ships blocked in the port have left. Icebreakers can do nothing. They telegraphed to inform the Chinese ships in Shanghai to postpone their trips to Tianjin for the time being.

Domestic Goods Transportation Should Use Domestic Ships

▲Ministry of Communications Orders Shipping Association

In view of the fact that foreign shipping companies are gradually expanding their business and arbitrarily sailing on inland rivers, which has greatly affected Chinese shipping merchants, and that the Chinese people do not pay enough attention to the promotion of domestic goods, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce specially convened the National Industry and Commerce Conference last year and proposed that domestic goods and company items should be transported by domestic shipping companies first. The proposal was passed by the conference and requested that the Ministries of Communications and Industry and Commerce jointly handle it. Yesterday, the Shanghai Shipping Association received an order from the Ministry of Communications saying, "In order to comply with the order, it is hereby informed that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has consulted regarding the Industry and Commerce Conference in the file of the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce, regarding shipping matters, including the proposal submitted by this Ministry that domestic goods and public goods should be transported by domestic shipping companies first. The conference resolved to consult and request joint handling, etc. In this regard, after investigation, items two and three of the original proposal should be submitted to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance for verification and handling by this Ministry and the Ministry of Industry separately. Item one of the proposal, in addition to being notified by the Ministry of Industry to the industrial and commercial organizations in various provinces for compliance, is hereby copied and issued to the association for forwarding to all shipping companies for their information. This order, etc." After receiving the order, the association immediately notified all members to investigate and comply.

All Companies Must Report Election of Directors and Supervisors

▲Order from the Ministry of Industry

Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industry stated that when the term of office of the directors and supervisors of registered companies expires, they should be re-elected and reported for record. However, many companies are still unaware of this procedure. Therefore, order No. 2324 was issued, which stated, "In order to order matters, it is found that when the term of office of the directors and supervisors of each company expires, they should be re-elected and reported for record. This company has not reported since it was approved for registration, which is inappropriate. It should be known that the directors and supervisors are the representatives of the company. If they are not reported for record, the impact will be huge. The company is hereby ordered to report the names and addresses of the current directors and supervisors, as well as the number of shares held, within ten days of receiving this order, without any delay. This order," etc.

Meeting Record of the People's Livelihood Research Association

▲First Discussion Meeting Yesterday

The People's Livelihood Improvement Research Association continued to meet at 23 Yuanmingyuan Road yesterday, holding two sessions, one in the morning and one in the afternoon. More than 60 representatives from various places attended. Chen Liting chaired the meeting in the morning, and Chen Qitian chaired the meeting in the afternoon. The situation is recorded as follows:

▲Reports: (1) Qian Genya and Baimili (transliteration) reported on the situation of workers in cotton mills. (2) Tan Baizhi reported on the situation of railway workers. (3) Wang Zhenchang reported on the living conditions of the poor in Shanghai. (4) Gao Naitong reported on the situation of workers in the Jingdezhen porcelain industry in Jiangxi.

▲Discussion Items: The topic of discussion yesterday was the key points of the living conditions of workers, divided into four categories: (A) Income: (1) Low wages; (2) Instability and unemployment; (B) Working Conditions: (1) Long working hours; (2) Danger of injury, toxic gas, and accidents; (C) Living Conditions: (1) Poor housing; (2) Lack of proper entertainment, inability to use free time well; (D) Workers' Concepts: (1) Lack of educational opportunities; (2) Taking fate as the standard. The discussion resulted in attention to the following points: (1) Food: Research on foods that are inexpensive and nutritious; (2) Housing: Take high, dry, and hygienic conditions as the standard; (3) Establish mutual aid societies to handle credit and lending; (4) Invest in public utilities; (5) Organize groups to achieve the purpose of workers' lives. Finally, Tan Baizhi proposed to pay attention to workers' morality and knowledge. Ms. Deng proposed to improve and enhance workers' desires in life.

▲Today's Agenda: The topic of discussion today is worker education. The topics are the Chinese labor problem and the International Labor Organization.

Central Government Abolishes Regulations on the Organization of Farmers' Associations

▲City Party Headquarters Complies with Order

The Farmers' Association Law and the implementing regulations of the Farmers' Association Law were promulgated and implemented by the National Government on December 30th of last year and January 31st of this year, respectively. The regulations on the organization of farmers' associations promulgated on July 7th of the 17th year of the Republic of China (1928) were also abolished by the 125th Standing Committee of the Central Government. From now on, all farmers' organizations in various places should be reorganized or organized in accordance with the new law. The Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipality Party Headquarters has received the above order and has forwarded it to all districts yesterday for their information. It is also reported that the Training Department of the Central Government has prepared a method for provincial and special municipality party headquarters and county and city party headquarters to guide the organization of farmers' associations, which has also been submitted to and passed by the 126th Standing Committee of the Central Government and promulgated to party headquarters in various places for compliance and guidance. After receiving this order, the Executive Committee of the city has handed it over to the Civil Training Committee for handling.

Two Railways Restrict Year-End Salary Increases for Employees

Employees of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways who have no faults during the year are entitled to a salary increase at the end of each year in accordance with their position and grade, as a reward. Indirectly, this can make employees work diligently and abide by the rules cautiously. Therefore, employees who have been serving for a long time without any faults, even if their positions are not superior, can still serve with peace of mind, thanks to this. It is now heard that in the future, those who have no special achievements will not be allowed to request a salary increase at will. Even if their achievements are particularly outstanding and there are facts to prove it, it must be stated before they can enjoy a salary increase.

Anhui Association Asks to Prohibit Opium by Telegram

(1) To the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Control Yuan, the Ministry of Interior, and the Anti-Opium Commission: The rumor of opium monopoly is rampant, causing widespread suspicion and opposition among the people. This is a line of righteousness. We earnestly hope that the government will adhere to the policy of prohibition and not be taken advantage of by corrupt elements, causing international shame again. It is found that Anhui Province completely prohibited opium during the tenure of Governor Bo Qian in the second year of the Republic of China (1913). Westerners transported opium through the provincial capital, but were defeated by justice and eventually burned. Domestically, the opium seedlings in various counties were strictly eradicated. Opium offenders fled at the news, making Anhui the first province to report the prohibition. After 1923, warlords took turns to profit from opium. For more than ten years, they have been following the bad habits. Now, northern Anhui has become the richest source of opium production, and western Anhui has become the area with the most red pills. The people are emaciated and pale, but there is no Zheng Xia to draw a picture. Lucrative posts have led to disputes over territory. People are the fish, and the officials are the knife and chopping board. Even under the white flag, party members and officials openly compete to collect opium taxes, without shame. Although no reports of prohibition have been heard from other provinces, no Anhui person feels more ashamed than this. Our government has long suffered deeply from the opium aggression of imperialism, and has inherited the Prime Minister's legacy of opium prohibition. It has set up special agencies to implement the determination to prohibit opium. The people are also stretching their necks and toes, hoping for the government's new plan. The prohibition policy should start in Anhui. At the same time, we also hope that the government will severely punish the opium dens in the evil concessions to eliminate the source. The people are fortunate, and the international community is fortunate. The Anhui Association in Shanghai bows in submission. (2) To Chairman Chen of the Anhui Provincial Government: The rumor of opium monopoly is rampant, causing widespread opposition among the people. Since the Central Government has not explicitly ordered a public sale, it will of course implement the policy of prohibition. Anhui was already a prohibited province in the second year of the Republic of China (1913). Since then, there have been successive disturbances. Not only have government orders been abolished, but opium has also spread. Foreigners regard us as an opium-producing area, which is extremely shameful. We earnestly request that you comply with the Prime Minister's legacy of opium prohibition, giving the people a way to rehabilitate themselves. Local officials, such as county governments and public security bureaus, are most likely to harbor evil. They should be strictly investigated. If there are any violations of the opium prohibition, they should be dismissed and punished. The people should also be allowed to file accusations in accordance with the complaint procedures in order to purify the officialdom and clean up the government. The country is fortunate, and the people are fortunate. The Anhui Association in Shanghai bows in submission.

New Sassoon & Co. Sues Tenants in Qingyun Lane

▲ Lawsuit to Recover Unpaid Rent and Evict Tenants

▲ 164 Households Sued

▲ Court Schedules Daily Hearings Due to Large Number of Defendants

▲ Lawyer Xue Corrects Legal Procedures

The properties in Qingyun Lane, North Sichuan Road, are owned by the British firm New Sassoon & Co. The buildings were constructed only thirteen or fourteen years ago and are not yet considered old. Last summer, the company notified the tenants to vacate the premises for demolition and reconstruction. However, the 164 households refused, reasoning that rents would inevitably increase after the renovation. As the houses were not damaged and provided sufficient shelter from the wind and rain, they requested the landlord to postpone the demolition and offered to pay slightly higher rents. The landlord refused and hired over two hundred White Russians to demolish the houses. The tenants, greatly angered, accused the company's comprador, Xing Dingcheng, of instigating the matter and sued him in the Special District Court. The criminal court found the accusations unsubstantiated and acquitted Xing. The tenants appealed to the High Court, which upheld the original verdict. However, since the lawsuit began, the tenants had not paid their monthly rent, and New Sassoon had not sent anyone to collect it, resulting in arrears of seven or eight months as of the end of January. The company has now sued the 164 households in the Special Court for unpaid rent and is seeking a court order for their eviction. Judge Zhou Daren is presiding over the case. Due to the large number of defendants, Judge Zhou has divided them into four groups, with forty-one households summoned for trial each day, starting yesterday morning, for four consecutive days. The tenants were initially unaware of this arrangement, so almost all of them appeared in court for the first hearing yesterday morning. At 9:30 a.m., Judge Zhou took his seat in the Ninth Civil Court and announced the division of trials into batches. He then instructed the plaintiff's lawyer, Mr. Goodfellow, to present the case. According to the lawyer's translation, the Qingyun Lane area where the properties are located has become increasingly prosperous in recent years. The existing old-fashioned houses are out of place, so the landlord decided to renovate. On June 25th of last year, seventy-seven households were notified to move out by the end of August, and the remaining tenants were notified by the end of August to move out by the end of October. However, the tenants refused to move out and also failed to pay their rent. Article 450 of the Civil Code stipulates that a lease without a fixed term can be terminated at any time, provided that one month's notice is given to the tenant. The plaintiff gave two months' notice but the tenants still occupied the properties. Therefore, the lawsuit was filed. Mr. Sherman of New Sassoon & Co. testified that he was in charge of real estate at the company. Some of the houses were built seventeen years ago, and some fourteen years ago. They now wanted to demolish and rebuild, so they needed to take back the properties. Old tenants would have priority in renting the new buildings, but this case was not foreseeable. The tenants who were summoned stated that they should pay the rent, but unanimously refused to move out, and retained lawyer Yan Jiaqi for their defense. Lawyer Yan presented three points for the court to decide first: (1) The amounts of unpaid rent claimed by the plaintiff, such as those from Qiantai Xing Senji, exceeded one or two thousand yuan, which constitutes a district-level case, while the remaining debts were less than one thousand yuan, which constitutes an elementary-level case. Now they are jointly sued, without distinguishing the levels, violating the legal procedure. Moreover, cases of the elementary level, since January 1st of this year, should first go through mediation, but the plaintiff has not made such a request, and instead directly filed a joint lawsuit, which clearly violates the law. (2) New Sassoon & Co. is not registered in China and is therefore not a legal person. Therefore, its lawsuit should be represented by a manager. According to Xing Dingcheng's previous testimony, the company's general manager is named David and the second manager is named Collaco. There was no mention of Sherman. Sherman's qualification to represent the lawsuit still needs to be examined. (3) Some of the defendants are business names, but the plaintiff only sued the business names and not the managers. This is also illegal. Furthermore, there are many errors among the defendants, such as minors, mismatched names, or names with only a surname or only a given name. All these three points relate to legal procedure and should be decided first before proceeding with other matters. Judge Zhou stated that he would consider the arguments on the level of trial and resolve them together, without making a decision first. He instructed the plaintiff's lawyer to correct the names listed in the complaint and asked Sherman to provide evidence of representation. The court was adjourned to March 23rd for debate. It was already past noon. The second batch of forty-one tenants will be summoned for trial this morning.

Rain and Snow Damage Vegetables

▲ Vegetable Prices in the Market Are Extremely High

Since the continuous rain and snow at the beginning of last month, followed by severe cold and heavy snow, the vegetables in the fields of nearby villages have been frozen and withered, unable to grow, almost completely destroyed. As a result, there is a sudden shortage of all kinds of vegetables in the markets of this city, and the prices of the few available are doubled. At the most expensive time, each catty of cauliflower was sold for 1,400 cash. Although it has been slightly cheaper in recent days, it still costs 600 cash per catty. Green vegetables have completely disappeared. Spinach currently costs 400 cash per catty, and celery costs 300 cash per catty. Moreover, the taste is not very palatable after cooking. According to someone from a vegetable shop in western Shanghai, the vegetables in the fields from both sides of Caojiadu to the west to Beixinjing, Huacao, and Zhenru are almost completely withered and disappeared. Only a small number of vegetables near the houses of villagers are slightly damaged and can be sold in the market. Therefore, western Shanghai has become a vegetable desert. Considering this area alone, the loss is estimated to be about 200,000 yuan. The villagers who rely on these vegetable gardens for a living are crying out in distress. Furthermore, the wheat and rapeseed in the villages will be greatly reduced in yield due to the impact of the snow and frost.

There is still snow accumulated in the fields, and the ice has not melted.

Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Finance Implements Collection of House Tax on Roads in Western Shanghai

The roads in western Shanghai, such as Robison Road, Caojiadu, Great Western Road, Zhoujiaqiao, etc., were built by the Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council outside the boundary of the International Settlement. The taxes of businesses and residents were also collected by the Council. Since the establishment of police stations by the Municipal Public Security Bureau, the Municipal Bureau of Finance, in order to recover rights and interests, sent personnel to collect the general tax from merchants and residents on these roads a few years ago. However, the merchants and residents believed that one business could not afford two taxes, so it was not implemented. It is now learned that the Municipal Bureau of Finance has decided to implement the collection of taxes since all sanitation construction on the roads in western Shanghai has been carried out in order. Recently, personnel have been sent to investigate rents as a preparation for the work. The proclamation issued by the Bureau of Finance is recorded below: Proclamation: It has been found that police substations have been established on Robison Road, Caojiadu, Great Western Road, Zhoujiaqiao, etc., by the Public Security Bureau, and the residents have been given considerable protection. All construction has been carried out actively, and the collection of taxes is the duty of the residents. It has now been decided to implement the collection immediately. In addition to sending a letter to the Public Security Bureau to instruct the police stations in the relevant areas to provide assistance when personnel from this bureau go to investigate rents, this proclamation is issued to inform all merchants and residents. When an investigation is carried out, the latest rent receipt or lease should be shown, and do not deliberately disobey. Sincerely, this proclamation.

The Development of the American Oriental Banking Corporation

The American Oriental Banking Corporation has been established for fourteen years. Its capital has increased from 445,555 yuan to 1,732,448.27 yuan. The public reserve has increased from 226,062.21 yuan to 689,022.16 yuan. Deposits have also increased. In 1929, they were only over 2.5 million, but now they are over 8 million. The net profit for 1930 reached 473,942.29 yuan. The total business volume of the bank is around 14 million yuan. The Tianjin branch had a surplus of 66,045.89 yuan in 1930. Last year, the bank expanded its business and remittance services in connection with Far Eastern and European and American firms, and its profits will be even more abundant. The bank is now operating at its new location at 29 Nanjing Road, which is convenient for transportation, has a large vault and secure safe deposit boxes, as well as the latest bookkeeping machines and calculators, which further enhance the bank's reputation.

Impersonating National Government Secretary to Kidnap Overseas Chinese

▲ Li Zonghua Impersonates Li Pan

▲ Conspiring Against Luo Baoqiang

▲ Sumptuous Meal at Da San Yuan

▲ Preparing Car to Meet Chairman Chiang

Detective Suddenly Arrives, Throws Him in Jail for Two Months, Still Not Convinced

Luo Baoqiang, a Cantonese native, has been running a sugar business in Cuba. He has considerable influence in the Cuban business community. Seeing that the motherland has been unified and politics are gradually becoming clear, he invited several comrades to raise foreign capital and start industries in the country. After returning to Shanghai, he stayed at the Dadong Hotel to discuss matters with the relevant government agencies. On the 20th of this month, Li Zonghua, impersonating National Government Secretary Li Pan (i.e., Li Xiangen), visited Luo at the hotel, intending to defraud him of money or kidnap him for ransom. Wei Jun discovered this and reported it to the Lao Zha Police Station. Li was arrested at the Dadong Hotel billiard room around 7:00 p.m. on the 22nd. He was sent to the Special District Court for trial yesterday morning. The process of this event is of journalistic value, so the details and the court's verdict are recorded separately below.

▲ Overseas Party Member. Luo Baoqiang is from Taishan, Guangdong. He has been doing business in Cuba, America. Luo is a member of the Kuomintang. In addition to doing business, he also handles overseas party affairs. Therefore, Luo has considerable influence not only in the business community in Cuba, but also in overseas party affairs. Last year, Luo, seeing that the motherland had been unified, invited several comrades to form a sugar company in order to operate a sugar business in the country.

▲ Sugar Company. The sugar company organized by Luo raised capital of ten million US dollars. Most of this capital was invested by foreign merchants. It was a plan to use foreign capital to start industries in the motherland. After the organization was established, the organization plan was forwarded by the Cuban minister Ling Bing to the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Minister Kong replied that it was adopted and invited Luo back to the country to discuss the matter in person. Luo received the telegram and returned to the country with four Cubans (i.e., an economic delegation). He arrived in Shanghai on November 4th last year and went to Nanjing to meet with Minister Kong. He returned to Shanghai on December 7th and stayed at the Dadong Hotel on the second floor, waiting for the government's approval.

▲ Uninvited Guest. Around 3:00 p.m. on February 20th of this year, Li Zonghua, impersonating National Government Secretary Li Pan, visited Luo at the Dadong Hotel. After the meeting, Li Zonghua said, "I am Secretary Li of Chairman Chiang. I was introduced by your friend Huang Dingzhi (who is indeed a friend of Luo and now works in the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission) to Shanghai to contact you about the sugar company." He also said that people in Nanjing were well aware of this large-scale plan and asked about its progress. Luo replied that it would be successful soon. Li said that the matter could not be expedited unless he personally met with Chairman Chiang. Luo replied that this type of industrial plan did not seem to require bothering Chairman Chiang. The relevant departments of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce could handle it fully. Li said, "If you see Chairman Chiang, this matter can be successful immediately, and I can do my best to introduce you. Chairman Chiang trusts me very much. Our relationship is like his right and left hands. I am good at writing and calligraphy, and I can write with both hands."

▲ Becoming Suspicious. At this point, Luo saw that his words were inappropriate and knew that he was definitely not Secretary Li Pan. Luo took the opportunity to ask him to write with his left hand. He was indeed able to write freely, and his brushwork was quite vigorous. At four o'clock, Luo asked him to leave his Nanjing address. The address he wrote was consistent with the residence of Secretary Li, but around six o'clock, Luo asked if he had had dinner. Li replied that he had not. Luo invited him to dinner at Da San Yuan on Nanjing Road. Two of Luo's friends also went with them. Before leaving, Li suddenly said that he was very sorry that the free train ticket he had brought to Shanghai had been lost. He asked to borrow five yuan for his train fare back to Nanjing tonight. He would send it back to Shanghai immediately. Luo gave him five yuan.

▲ Sumptuous Meal. At this point, Luo knew that he was a scoundrel, but he did not want to expose him, but still treated him with kindness. He went to Da San Yuan with him and they had a sumptuous meal. After eating, Li again said that Chairman Chiang was coming to Shanghai on Wednesday. He had to return to Nanjing tonight so that he could come with the Chairman on Wednesday. After arriving in Nanjing, he would send a letter to Luo first on Monday. Luo replied that this was good, and said that he would go to the station to send his friend Mr. Mo tonight. Mr. Mo went secretly to the North Station to investigate whether he boarded the train. The result was that he was not there.

▲ Second Visit. At 2:30 p.m. on the 22nd, the man went to the Dadong Hotel again for a second visit. However, Luo had moved from the second floor to the fourth floor. Li Zonghua waited in the billiard room downstairs because it was the route for guests of the Dadong Hotel to enter and exit. Around 5:00 p.m., Luo's friend Mr. Mo returned from outside. Li saw Mr. Mo and asked him where Mr. Luo was. Mr. Mo replied that he did not know, but said that he could call his friend to inquire and asked him to wait. Mr. Mo went upstairs to inform Luo, and then went downstairs to tell Li that Mr. Luo was coming soon and asked him to wait. He was also being polite and perfunctory. Meanwhile, Luo notified the cashier to report to the Lao Zha Police Station. At this time, Li said to Mr. Mo that he had three friends waiting together, and there was a car waiting outside the door. Because the Chairman had arrived in Shanghai, Mr. Luo had to come quickly, otherwise the Chairman would not be able to wait long.

▲ Detectives Suddenly Arrive. After receiving the report, the police station sent many Chinese and foreign detectives. Suddenly, they sealed off the billiard room, prohibiting everyone from moving and ordering everyone to raise their hands. The situation was serious and solemn. All the billiard guests were terrified and looked at each other in dismay. Mr. Mo pointed out Li Zonghua and said that there were three accomplices. At this time, three onlookers were sitting on the same chair as Li, and the detectives arrested Li Zonghua and the other three together. Luo also went along. After the police chief interrogated them, the other three were released because they were not involved. Li was detained. Li confessed at the police station that his real name was Li Zhongyue, and that he had been Secretary Wu Peifu. He was from Fujian.

▲ Sentenced to Two Months. The police station sent him to the Special District Court for trial at 9:00 a.m. yesterday. Luo also went to court to testify. Judge Luo opened the sixth court to interrogate him. Li confessed that he was selling calligraphy at the Dadong Hotel. Luo Baoqiang pitied his poverty, gave him five yuan, and invited him to dinner. He did not defraud him, and he was poorly dressed. How could he impersonate the Chairman's Secretary? After the interrogation, Judge Luo sentenced him to two months imprisonment on the charge of fraud. However, Li Zonghua stated in court that he did not agree and prepared to appeal.

▲ Catalogue of Huang Chujiu’s Assets

In short, the shareholder register should be pursued to the shareholders' meeting. Then, lawyers Chen Zhigao and Dong Chi said that the total amount owed by Riyue Bank Dashijie Savings Department was more than one million yuan. Since the announcement of liquidation, the accountants have collected very little from the debtors, which is very inappropriate, and should be ordered to pursue them as soon as possible. Wu Zheng and Pan Zhaobang should follow the court's instructions and submit it for verification.

Earth Guardian's Married Sister Sues for Division of Inheritance

▲ Earth Guardian Claims Sister is Not Father's Child

▲ Sister Claims Earth Guardian is Adopted

▲ Wood Tablet and Wedding Invitation Presented in Court

▲ Sister Requests Payment of 50,000 Yuan First

Earth guardian Wang Jinlan has a sister who is married to coppersmith Shen Linsheng. After Wang's father passed away, he left an estate of 200,000 yuan, mostly land. At the time, his sister wanted to share it, but Wang asked to postpone the discussion so that the estate could increase. In recent years, land prices have soared, and Wang's property has increased accordingly. Fearing that his sister would bring up the old matter again, he asked his sister to move elsewhere. Shen Wang's sister then asked lawyer Zhan Jifeng to send a letter to Wang Jinlan, formally proposing the division of the property. Wang also hired lawyer Tao Jiachun to reply, denying that he had such a sister. Shen Wang's sister then filed a lawsuit for division of the property in the Special District Court, stating that before the exact amount of the inheritance was ascertained, she requested that the defendant be ordered to pay 50,000 yuan first. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhou summoned the case for trial. According to Shen Wang's sister's complaint, she heard from her late father that the defendant was not his biological child, but an adopted child. She and the plaintiff, however, were brother and sister. The earth guardian argued that the plaintiff was born to the son-in-law of his maternal uncle, and was not named Wang. That the one she was married to was also not named Shen, but Zhou. At this time the plaintiff's husband, Shen Linsheng, came to court to say that he was indeed named Shen. Then lawyer Zhan presented the late father's memorial tablet, saying if the plaintiff was not Wang Yunzhai's daughter, then why would the memorial tablet be at the plaintiff's home, and that at the wedding, the wedding invitation was written and signed by the defendant. Next a worn out red wedding invitation was shown. Judge Zhou ordered the defendant to write the characters so the writing could be compared. Finally, after a debate by the defendant's lawyer, the court adjourned and said that the verdict would be announced on the morning of the 27th of this month.

Fan A'bao Accuses Zeng Ni Liujie of Seizing Property

丨Master-Servant Romance Produces Two Sons and Two Daughters丨

▲Ni Guangdong Flees and Doesn't Return

▲Ni Liujie Seizes Property and Refuses to Hand It Over

Fan A'bao, a woman from Changshu, is currently twenty-nine years old. When she was twenty years old, she went to work as a domestic servant at the home of Ni Wenbing, a Fujianese man who worked at the customs office at 748 Dixiwei Road in the Chinese-controlled area (formerly existing, now deceased). She then developed a romantic relationship with Ni Guangxun, the third son of Ni. Before long, she was dismissed by her employer, and so she established a small family elsewhere. Nine years have passed, and she has given birth to four children. Now, Fan A'bao has hired lawyer Yu Hualong to sue Zeng Ni Liujie (an employee of the Meiyi Company on Jing'an Temple Road, wife of a Mr. Zeng), the sister of Ni Guangxun, in the local court for seizing the family property and refusing to hand it over, requesting its return. Her statement roughly stated that since the plaintiff and Ni Guangxun formed a family and lived together, nine years have passed, and their love has been very close, with no discord. Therefore, over several years, she has given birth to two sons and two daughters, the oldest being eight years old and the youngest only a few months old (with photos to prove it). When Guangxun was at home, he cared for them all, except for the youngest who had not yet been born. The incident arose on the thirteenth day of the seventh month of the lunar calendar last year, when Guangxun, at the instigation of the defendant, unexpectedly left without saying goodbye in the dark of night. Several months have passed since then, and there has been no news. His whereabouts are unknown. The plaintiff was suddenly faced with this unexpected event, and her heart is broken. She looks around, bewildered, and has no one to turn to for help. Furthermore, Guangxun had no remaining family funds when he left, resulting in a lack of resources, and the young children have been crying for food for more than a day. In addition, the plaintiff is pregnant and about to give birth, making the difficulty of raising them even greater. This situation is unbearable for a weak woman. However, Guangdong was wealthy, and his inheritance from his father was quite substantial (about 25,000 gold). Because Guangxun was still young when the inheritance was received, it was all deposited with the defendant, entrusting her to manage it on his behalf. Guangxun had said this clearly when he was at home. Now that Guangxun has left, how can the young children be allowed to go hungry and cold? For the sake of survival, the plaintiff has repeatedly asked the defendant to return the Ni family's entrusted property in order to provide for her livelihood, and she has been mediated by others. The defendant also admitted to allocating 1,000 yuan, but this meager amount is not enough for the plaintiff and her five children to live on, so she did not agree to it. When the plaintiff had no other choice, she hired a lawyer to send a letter of demand, but the defendant refused on various pretexts. Her malice in coveting the property and intending to seize it is extremely obvious. The plaintiff cannot stand by and watch Guangxun's children suffer from hunger and cold. Therefore, she has laid out the facts and earnestly requests the court to show compassion for the weak and young, and to order the defendant to hand over all of Guangxun's deposited property in order to ensure their livelihood and protect their legal rights, etc. Yesterday morning, Judge Wang Qufei specially opened the Fourth Tribunal for the trial. The defendant did not appear. The plaintiff, Ni Fan A'bao, brought her two sons and two daughters and her lawyer, Mr. Yu, to the court. The judge briefly asked the plaintiff about her age and origin, and asked, "Who is Ni Guangxun to you?" The plaintiff replied, "He is my husband, and we are a married couple." The judge said, "The defendant's address is in the concession area, which is not under the jurisdiction of this court. This court will transfer the case to the special court for investigation." After the pronouncement, the court adjourned.

The Sudden Rise of Rickshaw Advertising

▲An Unprecedented Innovation on the Sea

▲Good News for More Than 10,000 Poor Rickshaw Pullers

The Baigao Advertising Agency at 36 Renji Road, recognizing the rapid development of the advertising industry, has pioneered the newest and most innovative rickshaw hood advertising. The far-reaching effectiveness and the deep impression it will leave on people are self-evident. The details of the agency's active efforts are described below:

▲Motivation for Launching the Initiative Since the introduction of rickshaws to the sea, there have been twenty years of history. More than 8,000 rickshaws operate in the city, providing a livelihood for more than 10,000 poor and struggling people. They are divided into day and night shifts, running all day in wind, snow, and rain, and their suffering is unspeakable. Last year, Feng Bingnan, a prominent figure in the Shanghai business community, felt compassion and published an opinion in the "Zi Lin Western Newspaper," expressing his sympathy for these poor rickshaw pullers. He took the lead in establishing the Rickshaw Pullers' Gospel Society, making a clarion call that resulted in a righteous cause. At the same time, he proposed that advertisements could be placed on the rickshaw itself, such as on the wheel guards and the back of the car, and that ten percent of the profits could be used to help the elderly and infirm rickshaw pullers. His intentions were both comprehensive and thoughtful. The agency's motivation for launching this initiative is based on this, and it has asked Mr. Feng Bingnan for guidance. ▲Great Efforts Made The agency, led by Wu Linjiang and others, has been preparing for more than three months, making every effort to carry out the project. It has created this newest form of advertising, never before seen on the sea. The hood used has undergone a series of scientific studies and is made entirely of canvas. It is installed on the rickshaw hood and is both beautiful in style and easy to install. The position for placing the advertisement is on the front of the back of the hood, with a blank space of 28 inches wide and 7 inches high. The advertisement is placed on top, and whether it is parked on the street or running on the street, it is clear at a glance and attracts attention. When it rains, the hood is turned up, and the front of the hood sits high on the top, with another blank space on the back for displaying the same advertisement. Therefore, regardless of whether it is raining, day or night, the advertisement can be seen all over the city and is visible everywhere. Moreover, rickshaws travel everywhere, through large streets and small alleys, reaching everywhere. Its effectiveness is truly a magical power beyond imagination. It is reported that a large exhibition will be held soon in the city, and the sudden rise of this new form of advertising will surely cause a sensation throughout Shanghai.

A Record of Old Feelings at Dinghu Yi Bing Zi Zai

Yesterday I passed by Maple Garden. Hong Shu showed me a scroll of "Records of Old Feelings at Dinghu". The painting was over three zhang long and was exquisitely made. It was painted by Zheng Wuchang as a commemoration of his close friend, Yi Bing. Yi Bing was from Jianhu and grew up in Linghai. She graduated from the Guangdong Women's Normal School. She was skilled in art, capable of writing, and had a noble character, looking down on the masses. At the age of twenty-five, she had not yet married. Relatives and friends advised her to marry, but she simply smiled and dismissed it. After meeting Hong Shu, they became friends at first sight and were as happy as if they had known each other their whole lives. Although Hong Shu had unspeakable personal troubles, Miss Wei was determined to associate with him. They enjoyed discussing literature and poetry. Later, due to other reasons, they parted ways midway. They missed each other in two places, and all they had was lonely poetry and books. Hong Shu cherished the memory of the past and painted the picture to express his feelings of longing. He could not help but feel like a wild goose flying at the end of the sky. Wuchang wrote in his inscription on the painting: "Miss Wei of Jianhu was exceptionally beautiful and intelligent and had a literary relationship with Hong Shu. However, due to environmental constraints, they parted ways midway. Miss Wei, though her wish was unfulfilled, remained determined. She was sad and lost her soul, and drifted far away. Hong Shu was also dispirited as if he had lost something. He went east to the sea, and when he occasionally spoke of the past, he would shed tears. He especially remembered the events at Dinghu in the late spring of Rensu. He then asked me to paint this picture to express his hidden resentment. I think of my deceased friend, Miss Yin Xian. The grass on her grave in Nanping is now nine years old. Loving couples are destined to be envied by heaven. Hong Shu and Miss Wei, although drifting to the corners of the sea and the ends of the earth, may eventually meet. Compared with life and death, Dinghu Mountain is high, but perhaps not as deep as West Lake." Before the painting, Yu Youren wrote the title, and Huang Huiwen inscribed the frame. The inscriptions and poems by Fei Zhongshen, Zhu Zhenzhuang, Liu San, Tan Pingzhai, Wang Luyi, Yao Mangfu, Jin Xihou, Yi Da, Jiang Jingan, Wang Qiuzhai, Pan Lanshi, Huang Binhong, and Liu Yazi further enhanced its value. Burglar-Proof Car ·Lu·Bing

A young British inventor named Feilanluo has a car equipped with burglar-proof devices. If a thief is not self-aware and attempts to steal the car, he only needs to touch the car, and it will automatically emit strange noises, as if clearly telling passersby that the car is being stolen. In short, even the most skilled thief cannot get his hands on Fei's car.

The Scottish court recently put a car with burglar-proof devices to the test. Everyone from the court was present, as was Fei. Fei first spoke, saying that this car was no different from ordinary cars, but it could prevent theft. The audience did not believe him and asked to try it. A detective came forward and tried to open the car door with extremely careful movements. Unexpectedly, as soon as he moved it slightly, a strange noise rang out, causing him to be startled and step back. Another detective claimed that he only needed to completely cut off the wires leading to the loudspeaker on the iron mesh to be safe. However, as soon as the car cover was opened and he was about to cut the wires, the sound rang out again. It is said that the above invention will be used on postal cars to ensure the safety of mail delivery.

Dog Matchmaker Chen Shuping

Dogs lying on the streets in the capital are everywhere. Although the Social Affairs Bureau once cracked down on them, ordering dog owners to go to the bureau to register and obtain a copper tag to hang on the dog's neck to distinguish it from wild dogs, no one took responsibility and the search was ineffective, so there was little success. In addition, many owners believe that dogs have a duty to guard the house, so they often keep them outside the door. These dogs then occupy the streets as their beds, and pedestrians often have the feeling that they cannot walk. The worst is the area around Gu Yi Lang, which is known as a village of vicious dogs, obstructing traffic, which can be seen in a glimpse.

One autumn night, the weather was cloudy. A fashionable girl with short hair, wearing high-heeled leather shoes, was returning from a banquet at Qi's house. Because there were no vehicles on the street, she had to walk. She was walking out of Mufu West Gate when she suddenly kicked something. It was as soft as cotton. The thing that was kicked suddenly jumped up, leaped over the girl's head, and made a strange noise. The girl was caught off guard and fainted in shock. At that time, Wen You Qing Hesheng happened to be passing by. He saw everything and quickly rushed forward to help the girl up and took her to a nearby dumpling and noodle shop. He asked for开water and gave it to the girl to wake her up. After asking, he learned that the girl's surname was Hu. She was from a prominent family in Jinling. She lived in Beimen Bridge. Qing Hesheng hired a car for her and accompanied her home. Her father now works in a certain institution. He has only this precious daughter under his knees and cherishes her more than anything else. He was grateful for Qing Hesheng's rescue. The next day, he specially held a banquet for Qing Hesheng to express his gratitude. In the middle of the wine, they talked happily. Qing Hesheng described that his family had a foreign goods shop. He graduated from a certain middle school and is now a teacher at a certain school. He lacks a suitable partner, so he still needed a wife. He revealed his intention to propose marriage. Although the girl's father did not agree in words, he already agreed in his heart. A few days later, Qing Hesheng asked a matchmaker to go back and forth to persuade him, and a good marriage was concluded. A wedding ceremony was held at a certain large hotel a few days ago. During the banquet, the guests urged the groom to tell his love story. Qing Hesheng firmly refused. Later, Mr. Zhang told it for him. The concluding sentence was, "The combination of the two can be said to be due to the dog's matchmaking." When the introducer heard this, he felt embarrassed and couldn't stop. It can be said to be fun.

New Trends in Sound Films Miaozi

There is a question that can give movie fans new considerations: "Which is better, sound films or silent films?"

Many people oppose sound films, believing that silent films have a "silent beauty." The actions on the screen do not really need sound to match them. The king of slapstick, Charlie Chaplin, once said, "The birth of sound films is the beginning of the failure of the art of cinema."

Many people also praise sound films, believing that sound films are indeed a special advancement in the film industry. The complex replaces the monotonous, the concrete replaces the abstract. Emotions are more harmonious because of sound, and actions are more intimate because of sound. Everything presents an absolute naturalness. Unlike silent films, which always make people feel empty.

Now, I don't need to explain which theory is correct. However, we know that sound films are not in opposition to silent films. Its subject is still the same as silent films, which is the plot of the film. Sound is only an accessory. Recently, an article by Dr. Mailun was published in an American film review magazine, which can well explain this point. He said, "Stage plays are stage plays, and films are films. If American film companies abandon the advantages of their previous silent films and want to use stage plays and song and dance as the central material for new sound films, then sound films will inevitably fail. What we want is that those who produce sound films should not make "sound" their first object. A tortuous plot and deep expression are still necessary conditions for sound films, and "sound" is only to add strength to those plots and performances.

Now, the film industry in Hualanwut (Hollywood) also feels this. Therefore, the sound films of 1931 are obviously different from those of 1929. So-called complete song and dance sound films are no longer common. And Lianyi Company (United Artists) actually plans to remake "Laihun" ("The Taming of the Shrew") into a new sound film. From this, it can be seen that new sound films have gained new awareness. In the realm of silver art, it will not be broken by the solid barriers of the original solid stage drama wave of song and dance.

Recently, the power of sound films has been unanimously praised by the film industry all over the world. In addition to the great success that the United Kingdom has already achieved, Japan also has more than ten sound films. Even in our country, although there is no official screening of sound films, the enthusiastic audience already know that a film starring Ms. Hu Die, "Song Girl Red Peony" is about to be released.

"Song Girl Red Peony" is completely sound. But it has not buried the advantages of silent films. Although there are many songs and dances in the film, the soul of the whole film has not been taken away by the song and dance. It has a very tortuous plot, depicting the fate of a song girl, full of the voice of the times. It has a very beautiful performance, depicting the background inside and outside the theater, exposing the cruelty of society. This is naturally a great success for sound films in our country. (Unsealed)

Travel Notes in Southeast Asia (125 Linghua)

On the twenty-fifth, I returned to Bosheng (Pathein). I passed through a county. There was no city. Most of the counties have no cities.

On the twenty-sixth, I arrived at Kangyidank. I was invited by the school teacher Zhang De. When I arrived, the students of the Gan Qidou Pingmin School welcomed me with a military band and cars and paraded through the city. This school has two or thirty students, mostly Lius. This village is very good. It can be called a model village. The trees are tall, averaging four or five zhang, and the shade is not hot. Facing a large river, it can be accessed by ships. It is one hour by train from Bosheng. The houses of the villagers are all good. Each is independent. It is quite suitable for hygiene. The roads are clean. Only the toilets are very inconvenient. Because of the rainy season, the ground is covered with deep water and no one cleans it. It's very bad. I gave a speech to the Chinese on national affairs.

On the twenty-seventh morning, I gave a speech to the students. There is also a Burmese Buddhist school here, as well as a Burmese high school Aided Natlnal High School. I showed them a letter in English. The principal, U Batin, immediately ordered the class to stop. All eight classes, more than two hundred people, came to listen to my "Great Learning" speech. I spoke in English, and Wu Batin translated it into Burmese. He very much approved. There was a female teacher, Daw Hta, who introduced her friends. In the afternoon, the son of Liu Xinxin, the director of Pingmin School, was fifteen years old and very lively. He used a small boat to send me across the river for a tour. I was happy to follow. Two children paddled a small boat that was eight or nine feet long and less than two feet wide. The water was like a mirror. We traveled three or four li to the other shore. To a Chinese family, growing gardens and reed. Six Pingmin school staff. Also, one family raises seven or eight fat pigs. The hostess served Min tea and snacks to the guests. She was a Chinese woman. We can know a glimpse of the living conditions of the Chinese in various mountain villages. The houses are simple, but people told me that the residents are quite affluent. The tea from Min Anxi is very beautiful. The cups are very small, no more than wine glasses, but if it is real tea, it is very thirst-quenching. However, the tea is bad and the cups are small, which is an obstacle for the thirsty. After half an hour, the two children still took the boat to send me back. This tour was the happiest. The two children also said that there was originally no duckweed in the river. I heard it was introduced from China. It looks very good.

On the twenty-eighth, I arrived at Daga Xinmin School to give a speech. Zhang De and Liu Xinxin and the students, as before, escorted me with a band to the station. We also passed two shops of the Liu surname. There is also a Pengcheng Hall. Everyone sent me to Dika. There are also many Lius in Dika. I did not have time to visit. I gave a speech on the progress of China after the revolution. Everyone was happy. I returned to Bosheng in the evening.

On the twenty-ninth, Chen Lianqing, the manager of the Kionmangne Electric Light Company, came to talk. We talked for five hours. We agreed to talk at night. We slept until the rooster crowed. I said. This is also a Pengcheng meeting. We stayed at the Pengcheng company. Mr. Chen knows each church and Tolstoy's theory.

On the thirtieth, Lin Chaoying suddenly sent a letter. Mr. Chen invited me to continue the study in Gongwenya. I was happy. We went to the boat together. The normal fare is one yuan. The boat departed at twelve o'clock and arrived at Miaoyu at five o'clock. It is a big market. Mr. Feng introduced me to Qiangya School. I stayed at the 工党 (Labor Party) in the evening.

Manuscript Examples for Book and Newspaper Introductions Three

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational, etc. books and newspapers are included in the introduction. However, books and newspapers that are not related will not be introduced.

(2) The pictures are limited to the latest works of new domestic and foreign artists and the attached pictures related to the text.

(3) Articles on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(5) The maximum number of words per article is 3,000 words.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw pictures, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and ink.

(8) Please indicate that the manuscript is submitted to the Book and Newspaper Introduction Editor for review.

(9) All manuscripts will not be returned regardless of whether they are published or not. If you need to return them, please state in advance and attach sufficient postage.

(10) The remuneration for text is divided into three types: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The same applies to pictures and photos. If there is a special manuscript, the remuneration will be calculated separately.

(11) The remuneration for text is divided into three types: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The same applies to pictures and photos per piece. If there is a special manuscript, the remuneration will be calculated separately.

▲The Triumph Hosiery Factory announces: Ladies who wish to make their silk stockings durable and long-lasting should pay attention to the following points: First, avoid pulling the sock opening too hard when putting them on, as this can damage the silk fibers. Instead, fold the sock opening down to the heel, then insert your foot and slowly roll the sock up, keeping it close to your leg. Triumph stockings have specially made edges for attaching to sock suspenders, providing exceptional comfort. For washing, gently knead them in lukewarm soapy water, avoiding vigorous rubbing, then rinse thoroughly in cold water, squeeze dry, and dry in a shaded place. Do not iron them.

Now that the matter is complete, I returned to Shanghai yesterday and am resuming consultations as usual. Hours are from 10:00 AM to 2:00 PM. After that, I will be making house calls.

▲Ren Nongxuan, an expert in Tui Na massage, Gua Sha scraping, smallpox and pediatrics, announces: I have studied infantile cold and heat, coughs, abdominal distension, diarrhea, vomiting, smallpox, phlegm, asthma, infantile convulsions, what Westerners call cerebrospinal meningitis, pre- and post-natal care for women, menstrual irregularities, etc. I have special insights and experience. I have been practicing medicine in Shanghai for over twenty years, curing countless serious illnesses. Lately, the weather has been erratic, and diseases are prevalent. Common infantile ailments such as fever, coughs, measles, and convulsions are arising at this time. I am a specialist in these conditions, so those seeking treatment come in droves. Hours are from 9:00 AM to 3:00 PM. No appointments will be taken after this time. My clinic is located at the first house in Fuyuan Lane, north of New World on Xizang Road.

Publishing News

▲The Liming Bookstore on Nanchengdu Road, Dade Lane, recently published

Page 22

"Chinese Finance Theory" by Yang Yinbo, director of the School of Finance at National Central University, is a meticulous masterpiece. With rich content and excellent printing, it can be called a magnum opus among domestic finance books. Since its publication, people from all walks of life have been rushing to buy it in an endless stream, which shows the value of the book. The book is available in three bindings: Daolin paper hardcover, priced at $3.20; paperback, $2.80; newsprint paperback, $2.40. It is also said that the bookstore will soon publish "Accounting Principles and Practice" (Frank H. Streightoff), jointly translated by Li Hongshou and Zhang Zhongliang.

Correspondence and Diagnosis by Yang Yanhe

To Mr. Wen: The condition of hernia has various forms, including rushing hernia, fox hernia, epileptic hernia, fainting hernia, 疝 hernia, 瘕 hernia, 　hernia, dribbling hernia, mass hernia, cold hernia, qi hernia, ship hernia, 胕 hernia, wolf hernia, water hernia, sinew hernia, blood hernia, heart hernia, liver hernia, spleen hernia, lung hernia, kidney hernia, yin hernia, heart wind hernia, liver wind hernia, spleen wind hernia, lung wind hernia, kidney wind hernia, fox hernia wind, running piglet hernia, food accumulation hernia, rheumatic hernia, and blood stasis hernia, among other differences. Without a diagnosis of your illness, it is impossible to speculate which type it is. The common prescription for treating hernia uses lychee seeds as the main ingredient on the left side and fennel as the main ingredient on the right side. Since the illness is on the left, you can use eighteen lychee seeds (one for each year of age), roasted until brittle in a new tile,

grind into a powder, and take it with warm wine on an empty stomach. After the first dose, take three qian of Qiaohe pills every night. If the leucorrhea does not heal, use three qian of Fenshuixie, decoct and swallow. Other accompanying symptoms require examination and treatment.

To Mr. Zhu Helin: For the treatment of "embroidered ball wind" (likely scrotal eczema), use a piece of salt-containing cattail mat ("one with salt phase"), about one foot wide and long, boil it in water and wash the affected area with the water. Save the water, heat it up again, and wash again, several times a day. After washing, apply Skin Fat Powder.

To Mr. Shen Yunshan: Incontinence with dribbling urine is called "Lin" (strangury), while clear urination with separate impurities is called "Zhuo" (turbidity). "Lin" has qi-Lin, blood-Lin, sand-Lin, stone-Lin, ointment-Lin, cold-Lin, heat-Lin, labor-Lin, and phlegm-Lin. "Zhuo" has white turbidity, red turbidity, stool turbidity, seminal turbidity, and white emission distinctions. It cannot be generalized. The prescription copied here only promotes urination and cannot be applied to everything. A single prescription for treating "Lin" is to decoct sunflower root and drink it, but do not cook it for too long. For treating "Zhuo", crush three raw ginkgo nuts (i.e., raw white fruit) and mix with water to drink. However, although single prescriptions can sometimes have miraculous effects, they are ultimately not as reliable as prescribing according to the symptoms.
